</tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\begin{equation} R=P+Q=\sum \limits _{i=0}^{162} {(p_{i} +q_{i} )x^{i}} =\sum \limits _{i=0}^{162} {r_{i} x^{i}} \end{equation}
</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>The calculation can be accomplished with exclusive-or (XOR) operation in hardware without carry transmission. The delay only comes from the combinational circuits, which is acceptable for hardware implementation.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6a2"><h4>2) Multiplication</h4><p>Multiplication operation is to calculate the result of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-524" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-525"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-526"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-527" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">s</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-528"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-529"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-530" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">s_{k}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>. width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-652"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-653"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-654" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-655"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-656" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-657"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-658"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-659" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-660" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em; padding-right: 0.303em;">mod</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-661" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-662" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-663" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-664" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 7.27em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-3.36em 1001.2em 2.105em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; right: 0.003em; margin-right: 0.003em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.2em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -6.483em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-6"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-535"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-536" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(6)</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.2em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -2.339em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-7"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-603"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-604" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(7)</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 7.27em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -3.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 7.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-35">\begin{align} s_{k}=&amp;\sum \limits _{\substack { i+j=k \\ 0\leq i,k\leq m-1}} {a_{j} b_{j}},\quad k=0,1,2, \ldots,2m-2\qquad \\ \sum \limits _{i=0}^{m-1} {c_{i} x^{i}}=&amp;\sum \limits _{k=0}^{2m-2} {s_{k} x^{k}} \bmod f(x) \end{align}</script>
</tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\begin{align} s_{k}=&amp;\sum \limits _{\substack { i+j=k \\ 0\leq i,k\leq m-1}} {a_{j} b_{j}},\quad k=0,1,2, \ldots,2m-2\qquad \\ \sum \limits _{i=0}^{m-1} {c_{i} x^{i}}=&amp;\sum \limits _{k=0}^{2m-2} {s_{k} x^{k}} \bmod f(x) \end{align}
</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>In order to reduce the circuit complexity, every time <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-665" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-666"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-667" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">a</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> can be multiplied with a small part of b. Bit number of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-668" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-669"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-670" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">b</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">b</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> can be set to one or more and the computation sequence of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-671" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-672"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-673" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">b</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">b</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> can be started from the Most Significant Bit (MSB) or from the Least Significant Bit (LSB). Furthermore, if the multiplication and the reduction are not finished together, extra register is needed to store the intermediate variables. For this reason, it is efficient to finish the multiplication and reduction in one clock round together. Another concern is how many bits should be used to do one round of multiplication. In the algorithm, in each round w bits are chosen from the key <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-674" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-675"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-676" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">k</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> to do partial multiplication, and then the following <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-677" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-678"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-679" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">w</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> bits of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-680" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-681"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-682" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">k</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> are shifted out to calculate the next part. Too large <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-683" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-684"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-685" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">w </script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> results in huge hardware cost, while too small <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-686" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-687"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-688" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">w</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> leads to longer computation time. Taking area and efficiency into consideration <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_6a2">[22]</a> and in order to meet the strict requirement of completing 1,500 authentication in one minute, 5 bits are the suitable choice. The calculation sequence is MSB because this sequence can reduce the number of modulo reduction.</p><p>The structure is demonstrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.5</a>. The input counter chooses <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-689" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-690"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-691" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">w</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> bits through the MUX, then multiplies it with A via network AND-XOR and XOR. The partial results are stored in a temporary register <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-692" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-693"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-694" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">p</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">p</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> and will be sent to AND-XOR network as an input for the next partial multiplication. A <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-695" role="math" style="width: 4.808em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.327em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.21em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-696"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-697"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.26em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-698" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">log</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.781em; left: 1.264em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-699"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-700"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-701" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-702"></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-703" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">[</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-704" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-705"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-706"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-707" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-708" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-709" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">]</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">\log _{2} [m/w]</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>-bit counter register adds 1 to itself after every clock in order to control the MUX by selecting <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-710" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-711"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-712" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">w</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> bits as an input. As a result, the multiplication operation consumes [m/w] clocks with the last result, indicated by signal <i>done</i>, being stored in the register module. The whole multiplication takes 33 clocks to finish if <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-713" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-714"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-715" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">w</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> equals 5.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota5-2615003-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota5-2615003-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">FIGURE 5. </b><fig><p>Multiplication hardware structure.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7583685/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6a3"><h4>3) Squaring</h4><p>The squaring operation means that operands A and B of the multiplication are equal. Though the reuse of the multiplication module reduces hardware overhead, the squaring operation can be implemented much more efficiently, using fewer than 33 clock cycles, than the generic multiplication operation.</p><p>In order to optimize the multiplication circuit, first, let<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-716" role="math" style="width: 17.42em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 15.679em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.084em 1015.68em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-717"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-718"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.285em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.02em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-719" style="font-family: MathJax_Size1; vertical-align: 0.003em;">∑</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1001.14em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.502em; left: 1.084em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-720"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-721"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-722" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">162</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1001.2em 4.207em -999.997em); </tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\begin{equation} a_{i}^{'} =\begin{cases} a_{\frac {i}{2}},&amp;i=0,2,4, \ldots \\ 0,&amp;i=1,3,5, \ldots \\ \end{cases} \end{equation}
</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>Using the conversion above, we can deduce the equation from the multiplication algorithm. The squaring module requires only 252 XOR gates with a critical path delay of 3T<sub>x</sub> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-851" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.14em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-852"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-853"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-854" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-855"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-856"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-857"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-858"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-859" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">x</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">\text{T}_{\mathrm {x}}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> is the XOR gate delay. The squaring module is a combinational logic circuit that can be executed in only one clock cycle. By this means, the performance of the ECC processor is improved with a minimal increase in area.</p></div></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6b"><h3>B. López-Dahab Data Flow</h3><p>The López-Dahab computation data flow is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.6</a>. (X<sub>1</sub>, Y<sub>1</sub>) and (X<sub>2</sub>, Y<sub>2</sub>) are two sets of operands in projection coordinates format for scalar multiplication. The left side presents the point-doubling operation and the right side presents the point-addition operation. According to López- Dahab algorithm, the present bit of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-860" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-861"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-862" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">k</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> determines whether (X<sub>1</sub>, Y<sub>1</sub>) and (X<sub>2</sub>, Y<sub>2</sub>) should be swapped. In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.6</a>, no more than 5 variables are required to be stored at a specific time because addition and multiplication can be done by X<sub>1</sub>, X<sub>2</sub> and Z<sub>1</sub>, Z<sub>2</sub>, T respectively. According to the modified ECC-DH protocol, only X<sub>1</sub>, Z<sub>1</sub> need to be communicated back to the reader in the end.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota6-2615003-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota6-2615003-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">FIGURE 6. </b><fig><p>López-Dahab algorithm computation process.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7583685/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6c"><h3>C. Control Module Design</h3><div class="section_2" id="sec6c1"><h4>1) ALU Control Mode</h4><p>In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.6</a>, only five registers are used to finish ECC scalar multiplication. The register file is designed in the format shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.7</a>. Assuming the data bus in ALU is m-bit width, five registers are connected to the inputs of ALU, and the stored value can be refreshed through ALU output. Certain signals control the moment to refresh registers. According to the López-Dahab algorithm, in every step, only one register’ will change the value while the others stay the same. So the ALU module selects which one or two operands in the register file should be used as the inputs for the operation procedure, then the ALU module calculates the result, places the result on the output wire via the MUX module, and tells the ECC_FSM module that the calculation is done. The ECC_FSM module asserts the<i>reg_select</i>signal to choose one register to replace the value with the <i>alu_out</i> output.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota7-2615003-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota7-2615003-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">FIGURE 7. </b><fig><p>Data flow of ALU control module.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7583685/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>This register file management has two main advantages: one is that no register will change value during the standby time, so the static power is low; the other is that the ALU module can easily choose which finite field operand will be used and where to find the operands. Compared with the Circular Shift File Architecture <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_6c1">[17]</a>, our architecture makes it easier to control the data flow and consumes lower energy.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6c2"><h4>2) Key Control Mode</h4><p>According to the López-Dahab algorithm, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-863" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-864"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-865" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">k</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> determines the value put into the point-addition and the point-doubling module, and <i>swap</i> controls whether the register file will swap the value in the register array. Additionally, the counter is controlled by <i>clk</i> and is used to determine when the calculation process is finished. If the calculation is done, <i>done</i> will be sent to the output.</p></div></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6d"><h3>D. Power Optimization</h3><p>Power consumption is one of the most significant restrictions of passive UHF RFID tags. Power consumption consists of both dynamic power and static power with total power being the sum of these two.<disp-formula id="deqn9" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-866" role="math" style="width: 100%; display: inline-block; min-width: 24.327em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; font-size: 111%; min-width: 24.327em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.066em 1020.12em 4.508em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em; width: 100%;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-867"><span class="mtable" id="MathJax-Span-868" style="min-width: 24.327em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; min-width: 24.327em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 20.183em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-0.958em 1020.12em 0.483em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; left: 50%; margin-left: -10.087em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1020.12em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 20.183em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1020.12em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 50%; margin-left: -10.087em;"><span class="mtd" id="MathJax-Span-872"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-873"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-874" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">T<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-875" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-876" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-877" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-878" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">l</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-879" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">p</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-880" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-881" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-882" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-883" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-884" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-885" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.303em;">D</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-886" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-887" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-888" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-889" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-890" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-891" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-892" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-893" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-894" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-895" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-896" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-897" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-898" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-899" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-900" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-901" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-902" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-903" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-904" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-905" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-906" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-907" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-908" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-0.898em 1001.2em 0.483em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; right: 0.003em; margin-right: 0.003em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.2em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-9"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-870"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-871" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(9)</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-54">\begin{equation} Totalpower=DynamicPower+StaticPower \end{equation}</script>
</tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\begin{equation} Totalpower=DynamicPower+StaticPower \end{equation}
</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>Dynamic power is composed of switching power and internal power. Switching power is caused by charging and discharging output load. Internal power is made up of short circuit and charging internal load. Static power is the power consumed when the circuit is in a stable state. For an ECC processor implemented in an RFID tag, power consumption optimization should be analyzed for both dynamic power optimization and static power optimization.</p><p>In addition to architectural power optimizations, traditional multi-clock domain technology and clock gating strategies are implemented <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref31" id="context_ref_31_6d">[31]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref32" id="context_ref_32_6d">[32]</a>. Multi-clock domain, in particular, is applied in the PWM module in the baseband.</p><p>The clock-gating structures are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.8</a>. The additional combinational logic can avoid dynamic power. The clock gating technique is mainly applied to the register file. At every state, only one register will change the value with the ALU output, and the other four registers remain unchanged. The application of the clock-gating technique significantly reduces the power consumption of register files.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota8-2615003-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota8-2615003-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">FIGURE 8. </b><fig><p>Clock gating structure.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7583685/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>In this paper, operand isolation is also adopted to reduce the power consumption caused by invalid transitions. The ALU module is taken as an example here.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.9</a> shows the comparison between the original ALU version and the revised power efficient ALU version. In the original version, when values on <i>aluin_1</i> or <i>aluin_2</i> change, modules ADD, MULT and SQR will work at the same time, despite only one module’s result needing to be changed. In the power efficient version, <i>sel_1</i> and <i>sel_2</i> are set to different values to induce expected changes so as to avoid the other two modules’ operation. As a result, power consumption will be reduced.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota9-2615003-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota9-2615003-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">FIGURE 9. </b><fig><p>ALU structure.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7583685/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec7"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VII.</div><h2>Synthesis and Verification</h2></div><p>The ECC processor presented in this paper was synthesized using the Synopsys Design Compiler targeting a standard <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-909" role="math" style="width: 3.907em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.486em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.49em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-910"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-911" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.13</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-912" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-913" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-914" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">0.13~\mu \text{m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> CMOS process. The power consumption estimation is generated with PTPX taking the node switching rate of the circuit into consideration rather than adopting the Design Compiler result. The synthesized ECC processor occupies an area of 0.3 mm <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-915" role="math" style="width: 2.285em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.99em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-916"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-917" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-918" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.3</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">\times0.3</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> mm. The synthesis results of area and power are shown in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a>. In the synthesized circuit, the <i>reg_file</i> module takes up 48.4% of the area. The ALU (including the ALU, adder, squarer, and multiplication modules) occupies 40.9% of the area, and the <i>alu_in_mux</i> module consumes 6.9% of the area. </p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table3"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TABLE 3 </b>
Synthesis Area and Power Report<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota.t3-2615003-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota.t3-2615003-small.gif" alt="Table 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p><p>The synthesis results show that the power consumption without clock gating is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-919" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1004.15em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-920"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-921" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">36.89</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-922" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-923" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-924" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">W</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">36.89~\mu \text{W}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>, and power consumption declines to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-925" role="math" style="width: 4.087em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.667em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.67em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-926"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-927" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">27.3</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-928" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-929" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-930" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">W</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">27.3~\mu \text{W}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> with clock gating. A primary power savings occurs by gating the output register to the ALU. Since the register only needs to store a new value when the ALU has finished its computation, we gate the clock to the output register to clock only when the output is to be stored. As a result, even though the register occupies a large percentage of the area it consumes a small percentage of the overall energy. The clock gate functionality occupies only 0.1% of the total area, however it reduces power consumption by 26%.</p><p>For verification of the ECC processor functionality, we utilize a Xilinx ISE 14.7 and Atlys FPGA board containing a Spartan6 XC6SLX45 chip. The reader’s command is simulated using the FPGA test-bench. The FPGA test verifies that the ECC processor can respond correctly to the reader’s command in a required time according to the modified ECC-DH protocol and the Gen2v2 air interface protocol. The tag clock frequency is working under 1.92 MHz and the ECC processor is running at 960 kHz in order to reduce power.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.10</a> shows the communication between the tag and the reader, and <a ref-type="table" anchor="table4" class="fulltext-link">Table IV</a> demonstrates the theoretical time required in each communication section. The reader sends the commands <i>Select</i>, <i>Query, Ack</i>, <i>QueryRep</i> and <i>Authenticate</i> sequentially, and the tag responds to the commands accordingly <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_7">[24]</a>. Because the encryption computation time is longer than 20 ms, an in-process reply is needed during the communication process indicating the tag is still working and the reader should not abandon the authentication command. At last, the tag sends back the encrypted message to the reader for verification. The entire communication and response process ideally lasts 38.6 ms.</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table4"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TABLE 4 </b>
Time Consumption Report<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota.t4-2615003-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota.t4-2615003-small.gif" alt="Table 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota10-2615003-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota10-2615003-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">FIGURE 10. </b><fig><p>Authentication process.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7583685/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>A screen capture of the FPGA verification measurement is also shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.10</a>. The measured time for the complete command sequence and response process is 39.6 ms. The additional millisecond over the theoretical timing occurs due to the inter-command spacing being longer than estimated in the theoretical model. This communication time can be further educed by not sending the <i>Select</i> command, since <i>Select</i> is ot required during every singulation attempt.</p><p><a ref-type="table" anchor="table5" class="fulltext-link">Table V</a> presents the results of area, speed and power consumption for our ECC processor design and other published ECC processor designs. In order to compare the various designs on an equal metric, the power on the basis of nJ/bit is valuated. The nJ/bit metric is used to measure how much energy will be consumed to encrypt a single bit during a single encryption period. Therefore, the processor designs reevaluated on their energy efficiency rather than the time consumption or reported power consumption. Even though <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_7">[19]</a> has a smaller area, it has a shorter key length and a longer computation clock cycle which results in longer computation time. Reference <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_7">[23]</a> has a smaller clock cycle number because it combines the addition and squaring module together to achieve high clock time utilization. As a result, it leads to more power consumption and circuit complexity. </p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table5"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TABLE 5 </b>
Comparison With Prior Arts<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota.t5-2615003-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/6287639/7859429/7583685/ota.t5-2615003-small.gif" alt="Table 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="table" anchor="table5" class="fulltext-link">Table V</a> shows that our presented ECC processor design as the best performance on energy efficiency. Note that our resented design achieves the lowest energy efficiency on the measure of nJ/bit, achieving 27% improvement compared with the second lowest design <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_7">[23]</a>, which is a significant improvement for low power RFID applications.</p><p>Though the size of the area and calculated clock cycle of our design individually are not the best reported, in combination hey demonstrate the area-time-power tradeoff needed to be le to operate in the stringent constraints of a passive UHF tag chip. Our ECC processor can meet the EPC Gen2v2 protocol in-process tag response timing, and the presented design is energy-efficient because of efficient combinational circuit design, system architecture improvements and low power design technologies.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec8"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VIII.</div><h2>Conclusions</h2></div><p>This paper presents a novel low power ECC processor design and modified ECC-DH authentication protocol suitable for passive UHF RFID applications. The ECC processor utilizes the López-Dahab projective coordinates which are’ adopted to represent the point on the elliptic curve. The ALU module is improved to be implemented in a small area, and the register file is improved to reduce power consumption during calculations. The designed ECC processor has been synthesized using Synopsis tools and functionality verified on a Xilinx FPGA device. The designed ECC processor needs only 12,145 gate equivalents based on standard <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-931" role="math" style="width: 3.907em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.486em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.49em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-932"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-933" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.13</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-934" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-935" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-936" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">0.13~\mu \text{m}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> CMOS process and consumes 5.04 nJ/bit during scalar multiplication. The ECC processor is capable of meeting the timing constraints inherent in banknote machines; therefore, this work is a viable ECC-based approach for tag authentication of banknotes during the machine counting process.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

Anti-Counterfeiting","abstract":"In this paper, we present the design and analysis of an energy-efficient 163-b elliptic curve cryptographic (ECC) processor suitable for passive ultrahigh frequency (UHF) radio frequency identification (RFID) tags that are usable for banknote authentication and anti-counterfeiting. Even partial public key cryptographic functionality has long been thought to consume too much power and to be too slow to be usable in passive UHF RFID systems. Utilizing a low-power design strategy with optimized register file management and an architecture based on the Lo&amp;#x0301;pez-Dahab Algorithm, we designed a low-power ECC processor that is used with a modified ECC-DH authentication protocol. The ECC-DH authentication protocol is compatible with the ISO/IEC 18000-63 (&amp;#x201C;Gen2&amp;#x201D;) passive UHF RFID protocol. The ECC processor requires 12 145 gate equivalents. The ECC processor consumes 5.04 nJ/b at a frequency of 960 kHz when implemented in a 0.13-&amp;#x03BC;m standard CMOS process. The tag identity authentication function requires 30 600 cycles to complete all scalar multiplication operations. This size, speed, and power of the ECC processor makes it practical to use within a passive UHF RFID tag and achieve up to 1500 banknote authentications per minute, which is sufficient for use in the fastest banknote counting machines.","isJournal":true,"isConference":false,"dateOfInsertion":"23 May 2017","publicationDate":"2017","conferenceDate":" ","isACM":false,"volume":"5","publisher":"IEEE","isEarlyAccess":false,"isBook":false,"isEphemera":false,"isOpenAccess":true,"accessionNumber":"16772304","htmlLink":"/document/7583685/","isDynamicHtml":true,"isFreeDocument":true,"isSMPTE":false,"isCustomDenial":false,"persistentLink":"http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/servlet/opac?punumber=6287639","isStaticHtml":false,"isNotDynamicOrStatic":false,"htmlAbstractLink":"/document/7583685/","isPromo":false,"journalDisplayDateOfPublication":"05 October 2016","chronOrPublicationDate":"2017","isStandard":false,"startPage":"3044","fundingAgencies":{"fundingAgency":[{"fundingId":"","fundingName":"National Science and Technology Pillar Program of China"},{"fundingId":"10.13039/501100001809","fundingName":"National Natural Science Foundation of China"},{"fundingId":"","fundingName":"Shanghai Pujiang Program"},{"fundingId":"10.13039/501100001691","fundingName":"JSPS KAKENHI"}]},"openAccessFlag":"yes","ephemeraFlag":"false","title":"An Energy-Efficient ECC Processor of UHF RFID Tag for Banknote Anti-Counterfeiting","confLoc":"","graphicalAbstract":{"summary":"An optimized energy-efficient 163-bit Elliptic Curve Cryptographic (ECC) processor suitable for passive Ultra High Frequency (UHF) Radio Frequency Identification (RFID) tags using for banknote authentication.
